    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer2159724469866384649">'Twas the night (okay, more like the week) before Christmas, and all through the tiny community of Pine Cove, California, people are busy buying, wrapping, packing, and generally getting into the holiday spirit.<br/><br/>But not everybody is feeling the joy. Little Joshua Barker is in desperate need of a holiday miracle. No, he's not on his deathbed; no, his dog hasn't run away from</span>
  <span id="freeText2159724469866384649" style="display:none">'Twas the night (okay, more like the week) before Christmas, and all through the tiny community of Pine Cove, California, people are busy buying, wrapping, packing, and generally getting into the holiday spirit.<br /><br />But not everybody is feeling the joy. Little Joshua Barker is in desperate need of a holiday miracle. No, he's not on his deathbed; no, his dog hasn't run away from home. But Josh is sure that he saw Santa take a shovel to the head, and now the seven-year-old has only one prayer: <i>Please, Santa, come back from the dead.</i><br /><br />But hold on! There's an angel waiting in the wings. (<i>Wings,</i> get it?) It's none other than the Archangel Raziel come to Earth seeking a small child with a wish that needs granting. Unfortunately, our angel's not sporting the brightest halo in the bunch, and before you can say "Kris Kringle," he's botched his sacred mission and sent the residents of Pine Cove headlong into Christmas chaos, culminating in the most hilarious and horrifying holiday party the town has ever seen.<br /><br />Move over, Charles Dickens—it's Christopher Moore time.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/196508-this-is-now-labeled-as-the-3rd-book-in-a">This is now labeled as the 3rd book in a series. Are they actually just stories situated in the same town and can be read in any order, or do they need to be read sequentially?</a>
</div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/29019237-michael"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/29019237-michael">Michael</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's not so much a series as they are stories set in the same town with many of the same characters. There are occasional references to things that ha<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's not so much a series as they are stories set in the same town with many of the same characters. There are occasional references to things that happened in other books, but nothing that spoils any of the stories. I read them out of sequence. In some of the earlier books, I had the "aha" moment.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31913085?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/219801-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060590253" href="/book/show/774806.The_Stupidest_Angel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31913085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13150033191516165576">What is not to love about a book that has a pot smoking law official married to a crazy woman who runs around naked with a broad sword, brain sucking zombies lead by Santa who want to go shopping at IKEA, incompetent arc angel who likes snickers, and a talking fruit bat? I found the story to be very entertaining with several laugh out loud points (I listened to it on tape). I’d recommend this book to anyone who can just let go of reality and enjoy a tale.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380123043?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380123043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17361639898699415725">Kitchen sink wackiness and a troop of tropes parade through a book not half as hilarious as I had hoped it would be. <br/><br/>In a barely fictional California coastal town -that's about two hours from where I live and, to the writer's credit, I feel pretty sure I've been there- the locals of a sleepy tourist town prepare for Christmas. A handful of middle-aged divorcees, lonesome loners, curmudgeons, and crazies bitch and bumble their way through a hair-(and more)-raising couple of days. A celestial visi</span>
  <span id="freeText17361639898699415725" style="display:none">Kitchen sink wackiness and a troop of tropes parade through a book not half as hilarious as I had hoped it would be. <br /><br />In a barely fictional California coastal town -that's about two hours from where I live and, to the writer's credit, I feel pretty sure I've been there- the locals of a sleepy tourist town prepare for Christmas. A handful of middle-aged divorcees, lonesome loners, curmudgeons, and crazies bitch and bumble their way through a hair-(and more)-raising couple of days. A celestial visitor scares the bejesus out of the local constable, who has got his hands full sorting out a town's-worth of mischief and mayhem. <br /><br />Do all of Christopher Moore's books include angels and an undercurrent of Christianity? I've only read two Moores so far, but I'm two for two on the jesus and god topic. I should look for titles without "gospel" and "angel" in them. So, that's on me.<br /><br />This isn't as funny as I'd hoped. In fact, neither of his books lived up to the hype I had built up after reading the reviews. I got a snort or two out of <i>The Stupidest Angel</i>, but generally I find his humor to be dated and easy, as in, he goes for the easy gag. Not that I could do better! All in all, there were a few insightful satirical jabs, but not enough to make me feel it was worth the read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17361639898699415725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoibhínn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoibhínn" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn">Aoibhínn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=humour">humour</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460864553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10749502123720214878"><i>The Stupidest Angel: A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror</i> was my first Christopher Moore novel. This novel is not the type of book I normally read. <br/><br/>The plot was quite thin but there were tons of funny scenes that made me giggle and snicker (it wasn't funny enough to make me laugh out loud). However I got bored with this book pretty quickly. The humour in this book is very "in your face" type humour. The humour was just so repetitive that it started to get on my nerves after a while and the jo</span>
  <span id="freeText10749502123720214878" style="display:none"><i>The Stupidest Angel: A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror</i> was my first Christopher Moore novel. This novel is not the type of book I normally read. <br /><br />The plot was quite thin but there were tons of funny scenes that made me giggle and snicker (it wasn't funny enough to make me laugh out loud). However I got bored with this book pretty quickly. The humour in this book is very "in your face" type humour. The humour was just so repetitive that it started to get on my nerves after a while and the jokes just stopped being funny. I didn't like the second half of the book as it just got too far-fetched and stupid. I really struggled to finish it. <br /><br />I don't think this sort of book is for everyone and I'm not sure that I'll ever read another book by Christopher Moore. He's the type of author I would get bored of very easily. If you like movies like <i>Scary Movie</i>, <i>Date Movie</i> and <i>Epic Movie</i> then you'll probably like this book. <br /><br /><br /><b>2 stars!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10749502123720214878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16705329467927869603">Its utterly rediculous, but its also laugh out loud FUNNY. Im listening on audio book and I've never enjoyed doing laundry more. Its totally odd ball, irreverent, immature, deviously clever and just plain silly, as are most of Moore's books. It doesn't matter if you find the story "believeable" its TOO FUNNY for me to care. <br/><br/>C'mon, washed-up female-battle-warrior cult movie star whos totally nuts (in a friendly crazy neighbor sort of way) married to pot smoking sherrif. DEA helicopeter subcontrac</span>
  <span id="freeText16705329467927869603" style="display:none">Its utterly rediculous, but its also laugh out loud FUNNY. Im listening on audio book and I've never enjoyed doing laundry more. Its totally odd ball, irreverent, immature, deviously clever and just plain silly, as are most of Moore's books. It doesn't matter if you find the story "believeable" its TOO FUNNY for me to care. <br /><br />C'mon, washed-up female-battle-warrior cult movie star whos totally nuts (in a friendly crazy neighbor sort of way) married to pot smoking sherrif. DEA helicopeter subcontractor helps woman he's never met clean up a crime scene, and introduces her to his pet fruit bat. Oh, yeah, and then there is the stupidest angel, and the sherrif's biologist friend who's doing some pretty wierd stuff with conditioning rats that just might work on him too... something about batteries and electrodes and underwear models... a little "goy" kid and his ruminations on whos got better holidays, and what's gonna get him on the bad list at the north pole. <br /><br />Kinda throws believable out the window before you even start the book. Its not something you'd want to discuss with the church book club, no worse than your average cable stand-up from a vulgarity standpoint and much funnier than most. I've been laughing for the last 3 hours straight. Its silly, go with it.</span>

<div id="review_1382769435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1382769435" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1382769435?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/12425422-the-stupidest-angel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1382769435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16480736959086128500"><a href='http://s61.photobucket.com/user/barklesswagmore/media/notamused_zpsrjf7fhiu.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471359185ra/20036115.gif' alt=' photo notamused_zpsrjf7fhiu.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/> <br/>There's nothing more to say here really. I'm throwing in the towel. I am on disc 3 and have been so completely zoned out I feel like I may have to go all the way back to the beginning. I don't know if I'm just distracted, completely humorless or falling into another slump but this book could not entertain me and I have far too many others sitting here to force it upon myself. The angel is indeed stupid as promised but so are most of the other characters (and there are MANY of them) and it's</span>
  <span id="freeText16480736959086128500" style="display:none"><a href="http://s61.photobucket.com/user/barklesswagmore/media/notamused_zpsrjf7fhiu.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471359185ra/20036115.gif" alt=" photo notamused_zpsrjf7fhiu.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>There's nothing more to say here really. I'm throwing in the towel. I am on disc 3 and have been so completely zoned out I feel like I may have to go all the way back to the beginning. I don't know if I'm just distracted, completely humorless or falling into another slump but this book could not entertain me and I have far too many others sitting here to force it upon myself. The angel is indeed stupid as promised but so are most of the other characters (and there are MANY of them) and it's all a little too wacky/zany for my current pissy mood. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16480736959086128500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_165448030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165448030" />
    <a title="Marvin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin"><img alt="Marvin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485672728p2/2160536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165448030?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marvin" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin">Marvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060590253" href="/book/show/774806.The_Stupidest_Angel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165448030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15753959699842515030">I just picked this book for our book club's December read but couldn't wait until December to read it. I guess you can say that a little Christmas mayhem is good for any time of the year. And if you think Christmas tales are rather lame, peruse this single paragraph at the beginning of the novel.<br/><blockquote>In another Christmas story, Dale Pearson, evil developer, self-absorbed woman hater, and seemingly unredeemable curmudgeon, might be visited in the night by a series of ghosts who, by showing him bleak v</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15753959699842515030" style="display:none">I just picked this book for our book club's December read but couldn't wait until December to read it. I guess you can say that a little Christmas mayhem is good for any time of the year. And if you think Christmas tales are rather lame, peruse this single paragraph at the beginning of the novel.<br /><blockquote>In another Christmas story, Dale Pearson, evil developer, self-absorbed woman hater, and seemingly unredeemable curmudgeon, might be visited in the night by a series of ghosts who, by showing him bleak visions of Christmas future, past, and present, would bring about in him a change to generosity, kindness, and a general warmth toward his fellow man. But this is not that kind of Christmas story, so here in not too many pages, someone is going to dispatch the miserable son of a bitch with a shovel. That's the spirit of Christmas yet to come in these parts. Ho, ho, ho.</blockquote><br /><i>The Stupidest Angel</i> is anything but the normal Christmas tale. Christopher Moore has revived the residents of Pine Cove, and some other characters from his other novels, with all their silliness and insanity and added an angel that is one part the Terminator and two part Jim Carry from <i>Dumb and Dumber</i>. This rather short novel has more one-liners than a Henny Youngman convention and more laughs than a barrel of tea party congressmen. I especially loved the return of Roberto T. Fruitbat from <i>Island of the Sequined Love Nun</i> but you do not need to have read any of Moore's other novels to enjoy this one. Put this on your Christmas list and hope someone doesn't kill Santa Claus before December.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15753959699842515030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478596315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11149164679819538408">3 ½ stars: It starts weak, you know that snarky humour that can wear thin real fast? Then he switches to crude. Crude done well can be hilarious and Moore’s a master. It’s a bizarre story packed with quirky characters, an action packed little page turner. Throw in a cemetery full of gossipy dead people, a murder, an archangel on a mission, zombies and a fruit bat. It’s even got a few decent though admittedly twisted love interests. My favorite the pot addicted cop and his warrior babe wife (a lo</span>
  <span id="freeText11149164679819538408" style="display:none">3 ½ stars: It starts weak, you know that snarky humour that can wear thin real fast? Then he switches to crude. Crude done well can be hilarious and Moore’s a master. It’s a bizarre story packed with quirky characters, an action packed little page turner. Throw in a cemetery full of gossipy dead people, a murder, an archangel on a mission, zombies and a fruit bat. It’s even got a few decent though admittedly twisted love interests. My favorite the pot addicted cop and his warrior babe wife (a loveable sword wielding psycho who hears voices). I thought it rocked until the ending, which was okay, just pointless. A fast, fun read. <br /><br /><i>"No one knows why, but second only to eating the brains of the living, the dead love affordable prefab furniture. IKEA!! IKEA!!"</i></span>

<div id="review_74078189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74078189?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandi" href="/user/show/811687-sandi">Sandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=funny-stuff">funny-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=2009">2009</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74078189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2965041803528304483">I don't think a book has made me laugh this much since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12070.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch' title='Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch</a>. I want to be the Warrior Babe of the Outland and fight zombies who want to eat brains and go to IKEA. I saw the movie <i>Zombieland</i> this past weekend and that might have just put me in the right frame of mind for this book.<br/><br/>Humor in literature is a very subjective thing. What makes one person laugh his butt off is just dumb and annoying to someone else. I love the humor of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14032.Connie_Willis' title='Connie Willis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Conni</a></span>
  <span id="freeText2965041803528304483" style="display:none">I don't think a book has made me laugh this much since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12070.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch" title="Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch</a>. I want to be the Warrior Babe of the Outland and fight zombies who want to eat brains and go to IKEA. I saw the movie <i>Zombieland</i> this past weekend and that might have just put me in the right frame of mind for this book.<br /><br />Humor in literature is a very subjective thing. What makes one person laugh his butt off is just dumb and annoying to someone else. I love the humor of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14032.Connie_Willis" title="Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Connie Willis</a> and I am amused by the Thursday Next series by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde" title="Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Jasper Fforde</a>. I've had quite a few laugh-out-loud moments reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10746.Jim_Butcher" title="Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Jim Butcher</a>'s Dresden Files series. Personally, I just didn't find <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide___1_" title="The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide, #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a> or the first book in the Discworld series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_" title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Color of Magic</a>, funny at all, but a lot of people I know love these books. So, if you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/74731.The_Stupidest_Angel_A_Heartwarming_Tale_of_Christmas_Terror__Version_2_0" title="The Stupidest Angel A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror, Version 2.0 by Christopher Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stupidest Angel</a> and hate it, don't blame me. We just might not have the same taste.<br /><br />I don't know why I haven't read any of Christopher Moore's work before. If this is anything like his other books, I now now where to turn when I need a book that will make me laugh.<br /><br />Oh, and there is a parental caution. This book is definitely R-rated for sexuality, language and adult situations. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060590253" href="/book/show/774806.The_Stupidest_Angel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Christopher Moore, other people who like to laugh</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Eric by: </span>
      Bobbi Madigan
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76688-eric?shelf=christopher-moore">christopher-moore</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer971822422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3905689422348483493">How else but in a mad lib could you have a book involving an idiot angel, a pot smoking sheriff, a zombie Santa, a talking fruit bat, and Kendra, Warrior Babe of the Outland? From the mind and pen of Christopher Moore, that's how!<br/><br/>This is typical Moore fare, which is to say, atypical, irreverent, and funny as hell. It's a short, quick read that never takes itself the least bit seriously, and, best yet, it's a Christmas story (I really hope they make a movie out of this, as is allegedly in the <a href='http://www.tsathemovie.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>wor</a></span>
  <span id="freeText3905689422348483493" style="display:none">How else but in a mad lib could you have a book involving an idiot angel, a pot smoking sheriff, a zombie Santa, a talking fruit bat, and Kendra, Warrior Babe of the Outland? From the mind and pen of Christopher Moore, that's how!<br /><br />This is typical Moore fare, which is to say, atypical, irreverent, and funny as hell. It's a short, quick read that never takes itself the least bit seriously, and, best yet, it's a Christmas story (I really hope they make a movie out of this, as is allegedly in the <a href="http://www.tsathemovie.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">works</a>. I would watch it every holiday season, assuming they didn't fuck it up).<br /><br />I honestly don't want to say more about the plot, because it's probably funnier if you don't know what is coming, but I will leave this quote, which comes from the end of Chapter One, to give you an idea of the tone of the book.<blockquote>In another Christmas story, Dale Pearson, evil developer, self-absorbed woman hater, and seemingly unredeemable curmudgeon, might be visited in the night by a series of ghosts who, by showing him bleak visions of Christmas future, past, and present, would bring about in him a change to generosity, kindness, and a general warmth toward his fellow man. But this is not that kind of Christmas story, so here, in not too many pages, someone is going to dispatch the miserable son of a bitch with a shovel. That's the spirit of Christmas yet to come in these parts. Ho, ho, ho.</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9785944416268045762">Ah, what to say about this book? I expected funnier. I really expected funnier. The review I read of this book made me (and my friends) laugh out loud. It was like seeing the trailer for a movie and laughing so much and then going to the show and realizing that the trailer had all the funny bits.<br/><br/>I did like the scene with Molly in the Pine Cove Bait and Tackle and Fine Wine shop. She was my favorite character in the book and I liked the scenes with her. Also, Christmas zombies are always good. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9785944416268045762" style="display:none">Ah, what to say about this book? I expected funnier. I really expected funnier. The review I read of this book made me (and my friends) laugh out loud. It was like seeing the trailer for a movie and laughing so much and then going to the show and realizing that the trailer had all the funny bits.<br /><br />I did like the scene with Molly in the Pine Cove Bait and Tackle and Fine Wine shop. She was my favorite character in the book and I liked the scenes with her. Also, Christmas zombies are always good. The conversations between the dead in the graveyard were fun - I wanted more of that! (And I know all the words to Good King Wenceslaus.) There were some funny bits, sure, but it just did not live up to my expectations. (The angel Raziel was from Lamb and I did like Lamb.) I have not read the other Pine Cove books.<br /><br />I think the humor was maybe a bit too vulgar for me. I think perhaps there was one too many penis jokes for my taste. I should just know what to expect from a Christopher Moore book by this time. (But I did like Lamb!)</span>

    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8201780-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412473145p2/8201780.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212424112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16403171981165134486">I generally enjoy Moore's comedies but this one's just too silly.<br/><br/>Raziel, God's stupidest angel has been sent to earth to grant a Christmas miracle to a lucky child. In the quaint village of Pine Cove, he meets 8 year old Joshua, a recent witness to the death of Santa (actually the accidental killing of local jerk Dale, in a Santa suit, by his ex-wife), who fears Christmas is lost. Raziel seeks to rectify the matter by raising Santa--and every other corpse in the graveyard--from the dead on Chris</span>
  <span id="freeText16403171981165134486" style="display:none">I generally enjoy Moore's comedies but this one's just too silly.<br /><br />Raziel, God's stupidest angel has been sent to earth to grant a Christmas miracle to a lucky child. In the quaint village of Pine Cove, he meets 8 year old Joshua, a recent witness to the death of Santa (actually the accidental killing of local jerk Dale, in a Santa suit, by his ex-wife), who fears Christmas is lost. Raziel seeks to rectify the matter by raising Santa--and every other corpse in the graveyard--from the dead on Christmas Eve. Chaos ensues, said zombies ultimately subdued--hacked back to death--by retired B-movie actress Molly, reprising her signature role of Kendra, Warrior Babe of the Outland complete with sword. If that doesn't put you in the Christmas spirit, you're just not ready for the holidays. Some fun moments, but no where near the cleverness of Moore's better books like <i>Fool</i>, <i>Lamb</i> and <i>A Dirty Job</i>.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_16903330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16903330" />
    <a title="Leslie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/224054-leslie"><img alt="Leslie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224126801p2/224054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16903330?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/224054-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780060738747" href="/book/show/1475288.The_Stupidest_Angel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like demented stuff</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/224054-leslie?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/224054-leslie?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16903330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17778406932548883354">If you're sick of all the sentimental Christmas stories and looking for something a little different and have a twisted sense of humor. This is the book for you. <br/><br/>My favorite scenes were when the dead people would talk to each other in the cemetery. I also liked how a lot of characters were very crochety and not shy about cussing. <br/><br/>Christopher Moore is the greatest at twisted, dark humor :)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36890125?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Serena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Serena" href="/user/show/1349220-serena">Serena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060590253" href="/book/show/774806.The_Stupidest_Angel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36890125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6749852873189655408">Christopher Moore's The Stupidest Angel: A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror is another audiobook to entertain, even at 5 A.M. on the commute into the city. My husband and I have gotten into a habit of listening to audiobooks in the car when we travel to and from work, and when we take little road trips.<br/><br/>Christopher Moore's books seem to be the most addictive for us even with the sometimes dark humor and harsh content. The Stupidest Angel is no exception.<br/><br/>The book is set in Pine Cove, Calif., </span>
  <span id="freeText6749852873189655408" style="display:none">Christopher Moore's The Stupidest Angel: A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror is another audiobook to entertain, even at 5 A.M. on the commute into the city. My husband and I have gotten into a habit of listening to audiobooks in the car when we travel to and from work, and when we take little road trips.<br /><br />Christopher Moore's books seem to be the most addictive for us even with the sometimes dark humor and harsh content. The Stupidest Angel is no exception.<br /><br />The book is set in Pine Cove, Calif., where the Archangel Raziel is set upon Earth to grant a Christmas wish to one child. That child is Josh Barker. Unfortunately, Josh has no idea what is in store when he asks the angel to bring Santa Claus back to life.<br /><br />With characters like a Warrior babe named Molly, a pot-smoking constable--her husband, a DEA helicopter pilot, and a evil developer, among others, there was nothing to do but sit back and laugh at the follies, misunderstandings, and interactions between these characters. Of course, there had to be a speaking, sunglasses wearing, fruit bat named Roberto! These characters stumble around in their relationships with one another, insulting their spouses and their friends, only to make up in the end, but the ride is raucous.<br /><br />It gets even crazier in Pine Cover when Molly goes off her medications and starts hearing the narrator in her head, giving her direction. She wonders off into the woods naked and carrying a Japanese sword where she meets Raziel who only wants to eat the marshmallows out of the cocoa packets. Meanwhile, zombies are raging war against the townspeople at the Lonesome Christmas celebration in the local church. The resolution to this story is truly in the Christmas spirit, but the ride to its conclusion is hilarious and action-packed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6749852873189655408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10794557644817120180"><b>The Stupidest Angel</b> really is one crazy, twisted book! This is the warning from author Christopher Moore just prior to the first chapter.....so take heed:<p>
  <i>"If you're buying this book as a gift for your grandma or a kid, you should be aware that it contains cusswords as well as tasteful depictions of cannibalism and people in their forties having sex. Don't blame me. I told you."</i>

  <span id="freeText10794557644817120180" style="display:none"><b>The Stupidest Angel</b> really is one crazy, twisted book! This is the warning from author Christopher Moore just prior to the first chapter.....so take heed:<p>
  <i>"If you're buying this book as a gift for your grandma or a kid, you should be aware that it contains cusswords as well as tasteful depictions of cannibalism and people in their forties having sex. Don't blame me. I told you."</i>
</p><p>Anyway, I did have a few laughs resulting from the freakish conversations between the undead in the graveyard, and did like Theo, the incompetent pot-smoking resident lawman as well as the bizarre church scene with the zombies, but it is unlikely this book will become a Christmas tradition for me.</p></span>

This is the second book I have disliked by Christopher Moore. His books are just too out there for me.         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060590253" href="/book/show/774806.The_Stupidest_Angel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4235780-chris?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4235780-chris?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4235780-chris?shelf=read-it-over-and-over">read-it-over-and-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4235780-chris?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4235780-chris?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119715102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12355277346574123953">Time to start reviewing some of my seasonal favorites, starting with my absolute favorite Christmas book, at least my favorite modern Christmas book. Subtitled <i>A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror,</i> this book doesn't stint on the seasonally heartwarming. Or the terror. Or the laughs!<br/><br/><i>"Fear not...for I bring you tidings of great joy. Behold, your Christmas wish has been granted...Not what I would have wished for..."</i><br/><br/>By the time Raziel, the common sense challenged angel of the title, makes this pr</span>
  <span id="freeText12355277346574123953" style="display:none">Time to start reviewing some of my seasonal favorites, starting with my absolute favorite Christmas book, at least my favorite modern Christmas book. Subtitled <i>A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror,</i> this book doesn't stint on the seasonally heartwarming. Or the terror. Or the laughs!<br /><br /><i>"Fear not...for I bring you tidings of great joy. Behold, your Christmas wish has been granted...Not what I would have wished for..."</i><br /><br />By the time Raziel, the common sense challenged angel of the title, makes this proclamation, a bizarre cautionary tale has spun out. In this season of not just giving, but of <i>asking Santa for stuff,</i> being careful what you ask for is excellent advice. Even the simplest wish can have unintended consequences.<br /><br />Christmas is coming, and in this neck of the woods...<br /><i>"Christmas crept into Pine Cove like a creeping Christmas thing: dragging garland, ribbon, and sleigh bells, oozing eggnog, reeking of pine, and threatening festive doom like a cold sore under the mistletoe."</i><br /><br />Into this cozy setting comes Raziel, a Nativity angel on a mission to fulfill the Christmas wish of a child. He finds Josh, who believes he has seen Santa Claus killed (in reality, a local asswipe in a Santa suit). And he wishes...<br /><br />I don't want to spoil the ensuing mayhem other than to say I can't believe I didn't figure out this <i>particular</i> part of the chaos until it was actually spelled out that this tale would involve...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[zombeeeez! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />A subplot of the book alludes to one of my favorite Christmas classics, <i>The Gift of the Magi.</i> It doesn't really give away much if I mention that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lena, former B-movie actress known for playing Kendra, Warrior Babe of the Outland, saves money by going off her antipsychotic meds in order to buy her husband Theo, a cop, a hand-blown glass bong, and Theo, <i>the cop,</i> starts his own little grow op to get enough money to buy Lena an authentic broadsword, which totally feeds into her Kendra-Warrior-Babe-of-the-Outlands delusions. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> See? Heartwarming! O. Henry would be proud.<br /><br />Anyone who has read other Christopher Moore books will recognize many of the characters from several of his other books. Lena, Theo, and the town of Pine Cove itself feature in <i>The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove,</i> Tucker and Roberto the Fruit Bat are from <i> Island of the Sequined Love Nun,</i> etc. Even Raziel the angel made an appearance in <i>Lamb: The Gospel According to Biff, Christ's Childhood Pal.</i> While it's fun seeing all these characters thrown together if you've read about them before, it's not <i>at all</i> necessary to know anything about them going in.<br /><br />Lastly, one small warning. The cover art could lead to the impression that this might, just <i>might,</i> be a book for children. It's not. In fact, there's an author's warning at the very beginning...<br /><br /><i>"If you're buying this book as a gift for your grandma or a kid, you should be aware that it contains cusswords as well as tasteful depictions of cannibalism and people in their forties having sex. Don't blame me. I told you."</i><br /><br />In fact, the phrase <b>"I-AM-SO-GOING-TO-WASH-YOUR-VOLVO..."</b> may enter your lexicon.<br /><br />Enjoy! <br />and<br /><i>
  <b>MERRY CHRISTMAS!</b>
</i> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12355277346574123953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2622066894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622066894" />
    <a title="Krista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4729639-krista"><img alt="Krista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579967825p2/4729639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622066894?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista" href="/user/show/4729639-krista">Krista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729639-krista?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622066894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15516286513398501575"><blockquote>
  <i>This was Raziel's first Christmas miracle. He'd been passed over for the task for two thousand years, but finally his turn had come up. Well, actually, the Archangel Michael's turn had come up, and Raziel ended up getting the job by losing in a card game. Michael had bet the planet Venus against his assigned task of performing the Christmas miracle this year. Venus! Although he wasn't really sure what he would have done with Venus had he won it, Raziel knew he needed the second planet, if for</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15516286513398501575" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>This was Raziel's first Christmas miracle. He'd been passed over for the task for two thousand years, but finally his turn had come up. Well, actually, the Archangel Michael's turn had come up, and Raziel ended up getting the job by losing in a card game. Michael had bet the planet Venus against his assigned task of performing the Christmas miracle this year. Venus! Although he wasn't really sure what he would have done with Venus had he won it, Raziel knew he needed the second planet, if for no other reason than that it was large and shiny.</i>
</blockquote><br />Having read, and surprising myself by enjoying, Christopher Moore's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28881.Lamb_The_Gospel_According_to_Biff__Christ_s_Childhood_Pal" title="Lamb The Gospel According to Biff, Christ's Childhood Pal by Christopher Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Lamb</a> some years ago, I was drawn to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/74731.The_Stupidest_Angel_A_Heartwarming_Tale_of_Christmas_Terror__Pine_Cove___3_" title="The Stupidest Angel A Heartwarming Tale of Christmas Terror (Pine Cove, #3) by Christopher Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stupidest Angel</a>; which happens to also feature the titular Raziel. As a mindless beach read with Christmas approaching, this book suited my needs precisely and I winced and cringed and smirked my way through it in a few hours. As an author's warning levels at the reader, this wouldn't be an appropriate gift for grandmas or kids (too much cussing, violence, and middle aged sex), and I suspect that I'm not the ideal audience for Moore's absurdist sense of humour myself, but I went with the flow and mostly enjoyed the ride.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> In another Christmas story, Dale Pearson, evil developer, self-absorbed woman hater, and seemingly unredeemable curmudgeon, might be visited in the night by a series of ghosts who, by showing him bleak visions of Christmas future, past, and present, would bring about in him a change to generosity, kindness, and a general warmth toward his fellow man. But this is not that kind of Christmas story, so here, in not too many pages, someone is going to dispatch the miserable son of a bitch with a shovel. That's the spirit of Christmas yet to come in these parts. Ho, ho, ho. </i>
</blockquote><br />This Dale Pearson – who seems to have had it coming – happened to have been returning from a Christmas party at the Caribou Lodge when he took the blade of a shovel to the throat, and because Dale was wearing a Santa suit at the time, a seven year old boy who saw everything believed he had just witnessed the death of Santa Claus. In a heartfelt prayer to God, this Joshua asks for Santa to be brought back to life for the sake of all the good little boys and girls around the world, and it is to grant just such a prayer that Raziel had been sent to Earth. But because Raziel is the <i>stupidest</i> angel, the whole thing goes wrong.<br /><br /> I understand that this story sees the return of many of Moore's characters from earlier books, and in a way, that's <i>exactly</i> how it reads: there are a bunch of very particular people, with hinted at backstories (the retired B Movie Queen who has gone off her meds, the pot-smoking Constable that nobody listens to, the crusty old bar-owner/nympho who could kiss or kill you at the drop of a word, the stranger to town with his talking pet fruit bat), and although these characters do all interact together, most of the action follows them as individuals continuing their own storylines (which I guess is what I would want to see if I had met anyone other than Raziel before?) But I will add that, just as I enjoyed with <i>Lamb</i>, there's nothing really irreverant here: for an absurdist storyline with a lot of fratboy humour, Moore doesn't mock God and prayer and people of belief; even Joshua isn't sure about God, but Raziel is obviously real and acting as His emissary. As a Christmas story, I find that appropriate. The ending might be a little weak (even with the bonus chapter that was added later to address this weakness), and the reading experience might have little value beyond a few hours' entertainment, but I was in the mood for something like this and it worked for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15516286513398501575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_249997124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249997124" />
    <a title="Megan Baxter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5742086-megan-baxter"><img alt="Megan Baxter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310153693p2/5742086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249997124?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Baxter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Baxter" href="/user/show/5742086-megan-baxter">Megan Baxter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249997124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8500801876901595637">This is the fourth Christopher Moore book I've read, and with the exception of Lamb, which I loved, the other three have evoked much the same reaction. I enjoyed them, I was mildly amused, occasionally laughed, but was left without passion for the books. (I often have the same reaction to Terry Pratchett, which may earn me no friends at all.)<br/><br/>I do enjoy them! I will probably pick another up at some future point. But I'm in no hurry to do so. When I do get around to it, I'm sure I'll enjoy it. But</span>
  <span id="freeText8500801876901595637" style="display:none">This is the fourth Christopher Moore book I've read, and with the exception of Lamb, which I loved, the other three have evoked much the same reaction. I enjoyed them, I was mildly amused, occasionally laughed, but was left without passion for the books. (I often have the same reaction to Terry Pratchett, which may earn me no friends at all.)<br /><br />I do enjoy them! I will probably pick another up at some future point. But I'm in no hurry to do so. When I do get around to it, I'm sure I'll enjoy it. But I don't love his books. They're excellent light fun, and sometimes that's what I want. But when I think about picking up another, there's no urgency. There's no little voice in my head saying "You know what you want to read right now? How about some Christopher Moore?"<br /><br />But who wouldn't love Christmas zombies? <br /><br />I also haven't read most of the books that this book draws on, so maybe that's where I'm missing some of the fun. But most of the characters are drawn clearly, if superficially, enough for me to keep up all the way along. And I love the fruitbat. And the dog. And mostly enjoy the Warrior Babe. <br /><br />And definitely the Christmas zombies. And their IKEA obsession.<br /><br />So if you're looking for a light, enjoyable book, this is it. It's a fast read, and a funny one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8500801876901595637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133303790?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlene Intriago" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlene Intriago" href="/user/show/3082173-charlene-intriago">Charlene Intriago</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3082173-charlene-intriago?shelf=books-read-2014">books-read-2014</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133303790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9315315564582439839">Parts of this book are incredibly funny but by the time you get to page 211 of this 306 page book, you know you are reading one of the most "warped" Christmas books ever! It is satire at its finest. It's Christmas in Pine Cove, California - just one of your typical little coastal towns that depends on the annual event for an influx of tourist dollars - but has a whole cast of zany characters starting with the town's only cop Theo Crowe (who has moved past his hippie days to become one of Califor</span>
  <span id="freeText9315315564582439839" style="display:none">Parts of this book are incredibly funny but by the time you get to page 211 of this 306 page book, you know you are reading one of the most "warped" Christmas books ever! It is satire at its finest. It's Christmas in Pine Cove, California - just one of your typical little coastal towns that depends on the annual event for an influx of tourist dollars - but has a whole cast of zany characters starting with the town's only cop Theo Crowe (who has moved past his hippie days to become one of California's finest)and his girlfriend Molly Michon who used to be the "Warrior Babe" in some B ranked movies. Throw in a whole lotta other crazy town folks and a few from out of town, the annual Pine Cove Lonesome Christmas party, an Archangel who has come down to earth for a mission that gets a little lost in translation, and an author with a really wicked sense of humor and you have a book that will have you laughing out load at parts and shaking your head at others. Definitely not your typical Christmas read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9315315564582439839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2426009732831208950">This has no redeeming value other than being entertaining & short with a dash of heartwarming. Pure snark, mildly amusing, & kind of fun, but the joke was wearing thin by the end. I'm rounding up to give it 3 stars. Still, it has Xmas, zombies, & definitely the stupidest angel. The best characters were the dog, the bat, & the psycho warrior princess, not necessarily in that order...<br/><br/>Yeah, it was kind of weird, but very well read. <br/><br/>I'm not sure, but I might have liked this more if I'd read the othe</span>
  <span id="freeText2426009732831208950" style="display:none">This has no redeeming value other than being entertaining &amp; short with a dash of heartwarming. Pure snark, mildly amusing, &amp; kind of fun, but the joke was wearing thin by the end. I'm rounding up to give it 3 stars. Still, it has Xmas, zombies, &amp; definitely the stupidest angel. The best characters were the dog, the bat, &amp; the psycho warrior princess, not necessarily in that order...<br /><br />Yeah, it was kind of weird, but very well read. <br /><br />I'm not sure, but I might have liked this more if I'd read the other 2 books in the Pine Cove series. I haven't. This is only the second book of his I've read, the other being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33456.A_Dirty_Job__Grim_Reaper___1_" title="A Dirty Job (Grim Reaper, #1) by Christopher Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">A Dirty Job</a>, &amp; I believe I liked it a bit more. In all fairness to the author, I don't seem to have the proper sense of humor for 'humorous' books. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gMCBPQ2nFE9tG4eUzqjonkLCDMBUb013uAj7UioiRzMiSBH5L0vt5XU9rFMciWhfmSFOHwcH9YMow87k0hmslQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

He grew up in Mansfield, OH, and attended Ohio State University and Brooks Institute of Photography in Santa Barbara, CA.<br/><br/>Moore's novels typically involve conflicted everyman characters suddenly struggling through supernatural or extraordinary circums</span>
  <span id="freeText1473654370297808117" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. </i><br /><br />Christopher Moore is an American writer of absurdist fiction. He grew up in Mansfield, OH, and attended Ohio State University and Brooks Institute of Photography in Santa Barbara, CA.<br /><br />Moore's novels typically involve conflicted everyman characters suddenly struggling through supernatural or extraordinary circumstances. Inheriting a humanism from his love of John Steinbeck and a sense of the absurd from Kurt Vonnegut, Moore is a best-selling author with major cult status.<br /><br /></span>
